Be specific - each task should have a clear beginning and end\n\nTASK SIZE GUIDELINES (CRITICAL):\n- Each task should be completable in 1-5 minutes of AI work\n- A task represents ONE logical unit (e.g., \"Create login form\" not \"Build entire auth system\")\n- If a task requires >3 file edits, split it into smaller tasks\n- Tasks should be independently verifiable\n- Prefer 5-10 small tasks over 1-2 large ones\n- Each task should have clear success criteria\n\nWHY SPLIT INTO TASKS:\n- Easier to track progress\n- Can resume if interrupted\n- Better error handling (failure of one task doesn't affect others)\n- Parallel work possible in future\n\nAVAILABLE TOOLS (use exact XML format):\n- <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>High-level goal and context</instructions></createPlan> - Create the plan FIRST\n- <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>Detailed step-by-step instruction for the model to follow when executing this task</instruction></createTask> - Add tasks AFTER creating plan\n- <updateTask><id>taskId</id><status>pending|completed|blocked</status></updateTask> - Update task status\n- <deleteTask><id>taskId</id></deleteTask> - Remove a task\n- <clearAllTasks/> - Remove ALL tasks from the current plan\n- <cancelPlan/> - Cancel and delete the current plan entirely\n- <viewTask/> or <viewTask><id>taskId</id></viewTask> - View plan or specific task\n- <listTasks/> - List all tasks in current plan\n- <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView> - Show directory tree. Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n\nTOOL USAGE GUIDELINES:\n(NOTE: The writing/editing tools below \u2014 Terminal, WriteFile, AppendFile, ReplaceLine, etc. \u2014 are BUILD-mode only. In PLAN mode they will be rejected. Use only plan tools listed above.)\n- Terminal: Use ONLY for one-liner commands. For complex scripts or data processing, use WriteFile/CreateFile.\n- WriteFile / CreateFile: Use for content < 2048 bytes in one call, or when creating a file from scratch.\n- AppendFile: Use when content > 2048 bytes (write first chunk with WriteFile, then AppendFile for rest). Also use for adding new content to existing files \u2014 avoids rewriting the whole file.\n- ReplaceLine: Use for targeted line edits. Specify a single line or a range of lines to replace with new content. Prefer this over WriteFile when you only need to change specific lines.\n  **CRITICAL ReplaceLine rules:**\n  - The parameter is <replacement>, NOT <content> or <contentOfFile>. WRONG: <content>Hello</content> -> ERROR. RIGHT: <replacement>Hello</replacement>\n  - Always ReadFile first to count lines and get exact line numbers (1-indexed)\n  - When replacing a block (CSS rule, function, class), include BOTH the opening AND closing delimiters in the range\n  - Example: to replace a block on lines 15-22, set fromLine=15, toLine=22\n  - After ReplaceLine, use ReadFile to verify the result looks correct\n  - **Edge case \u2014 last block in file**: When editing the final block (e.g. `if __name__ == \"__main__\":`), include the block header in the `fromLine`..`toLine` range. If you replace only the indented body, the header is left orphaned. Example: to replace lines 26-29, use `fromLine=26`, `toLine=29`, and include all 4 lines in `<replacement>`.\n  - If unsure about line range, replace fewer lines and iterate\n  - Multi-line replacement: put raw newlines inside <replacement>...</replacement>. Replacing 1 line with N lines shifts later line numbers by N-1.\n\n  ReplaceLine examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>12</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- TreeView: Use to explore project directory structure. Set depth=0 for unlimited depth.\n- General Rule: NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Grep / Find / List / TreeView: Prefer these XML tools over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- EDITING MINDSET: Just as planning splits a big job into small focused tasks, split big file writes into small targeted edits. Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. Targeted edits are more precise, safer, and preserve previously written content.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW:\n1. User says: \"I want a web app with login and dashboard\"\n2. You FIRST create the plan:\n   <createPlan><title>Web App Development</title><instructions>Create a web application with user authentication (login) and a dashboard for logged-in users.</instructions></createPlan>\n3. Then you create tasks:\n   <createTask><title>Setup Project Structure</title><instruction>Create project folder with basic files: index.html, style.css, app.js, server.py. Initialize npm if needed.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Create Backend API</title><instruction>Create server.py with Flask/FastAPI. Add login endpoint /api/login that validates username/password and returns JWT token. Add /api/dashboard endpoint that requires auth.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Build Frontend Login</title><instruction>Create index.html with login form. Connect to /api/login. Store JWT token in localStorage. Redirect to dashboard on success.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Build Dashboard</title><instruction>Create dashboard view. Fetch user data from /api/dashboard with token. Display user info and logout button.</instruction></createTask>\n\nWhen all tasks are created, tell the user \"Plan is ready! Type !MODE build to start BUILD mode.\"\n", "sessionId": 318, "rowId": 57, "timestamp": 1783654003.107375, "date": "2026-07-10"} -->

Use for content > 4096 bytes or adding to existing files. Params: <fileName>, <contentOfFile>, [<fromLineNumber>]\n- <CreateFile><fileName>testfile.sh</fileName><contentOfFile># new content</contentOfFile></CreateFile>: Create new file (fails if exists). If file exists and you want to overwrite, use WriteFile instead. Params: <fileName>, <contentOfFile>\n- <List><path>.</path></List>: List files. Prefer this over Terminal ls. Params: [<path>] (optional)\n- <listTools/>: Show all tools. No params.\n- <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView>: Show directory tree. Explore project structure, set depth=0 for unlimited. Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n- <ReadImage><fileName>photo.png</fileName><prompt>Describe this image</prompt></ReadImage>: Read an image file, inject into conversation for AI to analyze (vision model required). Params: <fileName>, [<prompt>]\n- <ExecuteScript><fileName>ls</fileName><args>-l</args></ExecuteScript>: Run script (.py, .sh, .js, etc). Params: <fileName>, [<args>]\n- <Grep><pattern>search_term</pattern><fileName>file.txt</fileName><recursive>true</recursive></Grep>: Search by regex. Prefer this over Terminal grep. Params: <pattern>, [<fileName>], [<recursive>]\n- <Diff><file1>file1.txt</file1><file2>file2.txt</file2><unified>3</unified></Diff>: Compare files. Params: <file1>, <file2>, [<unified>]\n- <Sed><pattern>old_text</pattern><replacement>new_text</replacement><fileName>file.txt</fileName><inplace>true</inplace></Sed>: Find/replace. Params: <pattern>, <replacement>, <fileName>, [<inplace>]\n- <ImageTransform><fileName>photo.png</fileName><operation>resize</operation><params>{\"maxWidth\":800,\"maxHeight\":600}</params></ImageTransform>: Transform images (resize, crop, convert, flip, rotate). Prefer this over Terminal find. Params: <pattern>, [<path>]\n- <Head><fileName>file.txt</fileName><lines>10</lines></Head>: First N lines. Params: <fileName>, [<lines>]\n- <Tail><fileName>file.txt</fileName><lines>10</lines></Tail>: Last N lines. Params: <fileName>, [<lines>]\n- <Sort><fileName>file.txt</fileName><numeric>true</numeric></Sort>: Sort lines. Params: <fileName>, [<numeric>], [<reverse>], [<unique>]\n\nPLAN MANAGEMENT TOOLS (use these to track progress):\n- <planDone/> - Signal planning is done, start the first pending task\n- <nextTask>completed</nextTask> - Mark current task completed, get next task\n- <nextTask>blocked</nextTask> - Mark current task blocked, explain why\n- <LogProgress><taskId>task_id</taskId><whatWasDone>What you did</whatWasDone></LogProgress> - Log progress on current task\n- <viewTask/> - View current plan and tasks\n- <listTasks/> - List all tasks\n- <jobDone/> - Finish the plan (only when all tasks are done or you want to end early)\n- <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>Goal description</instructions></createPlan> - Create a new plan (replaces current). Use when current plan needs full replacement.\n- <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>What to do</instruction></createTask> - Add a new task to the current plan. Always create a plan first.\n- <updateTask><taskId>id</taskId><title>New Title</title><instruction>New instruction</instruction></updateTask> - Update a task's title and/or instruction.\n- <deleteTask><id>taskId</id></deleteTask> - Remove a specific task from the current plan.\n- <clearAllTasks/> - Remove ALL tasks from the current plan (keeps the plan itself).\n- <cancelPlan/> - Cancel and delete the current plan entirely (same as deletePlan).\n- <deletePlan/> - Delete the current plan entirely.\n- <deleteDraft/> - Delete the unsaved draft plan.\n- <deleteAllPlans/> - Delete all plans.\n\nTOOL USAGE RULES:\n- NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Prefer targeted edits: Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. This is more precise and preserves unrelated content.\n- Prefer XML tools (Grep, Find, List) over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- For file manipulation with complex data, use WriteFile/AppendFile. For one-liners, echo/cat/tee with Terminal is fine.\n- Use ExecuteScript to run scripts you create (WriteFile/CreateFile). Terminal is for system binaries only.\n- Save useful commands and solutions as tips with <SaveTip>. Retrieve them with <GetTip>. Browse with <ListTips>. Bring saved tips into context with <ReinsertTip>.\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- If a tool returns an error with a \"Usage:\" example, the error message shows the correct parameter names. Copy them exactly \u2014 don't guess. This is faster than trial-and-error.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW (tasks from plan mode):\n1. Task received: \"Create project folder with basic files\"\n2. Use for content > 4096 bytes or adding to existing files. If file exists and you want to overwrite, use WriteFile instead. Params: <fileName>, <contentOfFile>\n- <List><path>.</path></List>: List files. Prefer this over Terminal ls. Params: [<path>] (optional)\n- <listTools/>: Show all tools. No params.\n- <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView>: Show directory tree. Explore project structure, set depth=0 for unlimited. Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n- <ReadImage><fileName>photo.png</fileName><prompt>Describe this image</prompt></ReadImage>: Read an image file, inject into conversation for AI to analyze (vision model required). Params: <fileName>, [<prompt>]\n- <ExecuteScript><fileName>ls</fileName><args>-l</args></ExecuteScript>: Run script (.py, .sh, .js, etc). Params: <fileName>, [<args>]\n- <Grep><pattern>search_term</pattern><fileName>file.txt</fileName><recursive>true</recursive></Grep>: Search by regex. Prefer this over Terminal grep. Params: <pattern>, [<fileName>], [<recursive>]\n- <Diff><file1>file1.txt</file1><file2>file2.txt</file2><unified>3</unified></Diff>: Compare files. Params: <pattern>, <replacement>, <fileName>, [<inplace>]\n- <ImageTransform><fileName>photo.png</fileName><operation>resize</operation><params>{\"maxWidth\":800,\"maxHeight\":600}</params></ImageTransform>: Transform images (resize, crop, convert, flip, rotate). Params: <fileName>, <operation>, [<params>] (JSON), [<output>]\n- <ReplaceLine><fileName>file.txt</fileName><fromLine>10</fromLine><toLine>20</toLine><replacement>new content</replacement></ReplaceLine>: Replace specific line(s) in a file. Use for targeted edits instead of rewriting the whole file. Params: <fileName>, <fromLine> (required), [<toLine>] (optional, defaults to fromLine), <replacement>\n  **CRITICAL:**\n  - Use <replacement>, NEVER <content> or <contentOfFile>. Wrong parameter causes \"Missing required parameter(s): replacement\".\n  - Always ReadFile first to get correct line numbers (1-indexed).\n  - When replacing a block, include its opening AND closing delimiters in the range.\n  - After ReplaceLine, ReadFile to verify. Multi-line replacements shift later line numbers.\n\n  Examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>15</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- <Find><pattern>*.py</pattern><path>.</path></Find>: Find by name. Params: <fileName>, [<lines>]\n- <Tail><fileName>file.txt</fileName><lines>10</lines></Tail>: Last N lines. Params: <fileName>, [<lines>]\n- <Sort><fileName>file.txt</fileName><numeric>true</numeric></Sort>: Sort lines. Params: <fileName>, [<numeric>], [<reverse>], [<unique>]\n\nPLAN MANAGEMENT TOOLS (use these to track progress):\n- <planDone/> - Signal planning is done, start the first pending task\n- <nextTask>completed</nextTask> - Mark current task completed, get next task\n- <nextTask>blocked</nextTask> - Mark current task blocked, explain why\n- <LogProgress><taskId>task_id</taskId><whatWasDone>What you did</whatWasDone></LogProgress> - Log progress on current task\n- <viewTask/> - View current plan and tasks\n- <listTasks/> - List all tasks\n- <jobDone/> - Finish the plan (only when all tasks are done or you want to end early)\n- <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>Goal description</instructions></createPlan> - Create a new plan (replaces current). Use when current plan needs full replacement.\n- <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>What to do</instruction></createTask> - Add a new task to the current plan. Always create a plan first.\n- <updateTask><taskId>id</taskId><title>New Title</title><instruction>New instruction</instruction></updateTask> - Update a task's title and/or instruction.\n- <deleteTask><id>taskId</id></deleteTask> - Remove a specific task from the current plan.\n- <clearAllTasks/> - Remove ALL tasks from the current plan (keeps the plan itself).\n- <cancelPlan/> - Cancel and delete the current plan entirely (same as deletePlan).\n- <deletePlan/> - Delete the current plan entirely.\n- <deleteDraft/> - Delete the unsaved draft plan.\n- <deleteAllPlans/> - Delete all plans.\n\nTOOL USAGE RULES:\n- NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Prefer targeted edits: Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. This is more precise and preserves unrelated content.\n- Prefer XML tools (Grep, Find, List) over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- For file manipulation with complex data, use WriteFile/AppendFile. For one-liners, echo/cat/tee with Terminal is fine.\n- Use ExecuteScript to run scripts you create (WriteFile/CreateFile). Terminal is for system binaries only.\n- Save useful commands and solutions as tips with <SaveTip>. Retrieve them with <GetTip>. Browse with <ListTips>. Bring saved tips into context with <ReinsertTip>.\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- If a tool returns an error with a \"Usage:\" example, the error message shows the correct parameter names. Copy them exactly \u2014 don't guess. This is faster than trial-and-error.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW (tasks from plan mode):\n1. Task received: \"Create project folder with basic files\"\n2. <!-- {"role": "system", "content": "\nYou are in PLAN MODE. You are architect. Your role is to analyze user requests and create structured task plans.\n\nMODE: PLAN (Thinking ENABLED)\n\nIMPORTANT WORKFLOW:\n\nPHASE 0 - CONTEXT GATHERING (MANDATORY):\nBefore creating ANY plan, you MUST understand the existing codebase:\n1. Call <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView> to see project structure\n2. Call <ReadFile><fileName>README.md</fileName></ReadFile> to understand the project\n3. Call <ReadFile><fileName>AGENTS.md</fileName></ReadFile> to understand conventions\n4. List and read key config files (package.json, requirements.txt, config.py, etc.)\n5. Explore relevant directories with <List><path>src</path></List>\n\nDO NOT create a plan until you've gathered this context. The user may provide files to read directly.\n\nPHASE 1 - CREATE PLAN:\nCall <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>High-level goal description</instructions></createPlan>\n\nPHASE 2 - CREATE TASKS:\nCall <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>Detailed instruction for this task</instruction></createTask> for each step\n\nPHASE 3 - FINALIZE:\nWhen all tasks are created, tell user: \"Plan is ready! Type !MODE build to start BUILD mode.\"\n\nHOW TO SPLIT USER INSTRUCTIONS INTO TASKS:\n1. Analyze the user's goal - what is the end result they want?\n2. Identify distinct steps that can be done independently\n3. Create tasks for each step with clear, actionable instructions\n4. Order matters - earlier tasks should enable later ones\n5. Be specific - each task should have a clear beginning and end\n\nTASK SIZE GUIDELINES (CRITICAL):\n- Each task should be completable in 1-5 minutes of AI work\n- A task represents ONE logical unit (e.g., \"Create login form\" not \"Build entire auth system\")\n- If a task requires >3 file edits, split it into smaller tasks\n- Tasks should be independently verifiable\n- Prefer 5-10 small tasks over 1-2 large ones\n- Each task should have clear success criteria\n\nWHY SPLIT INTO TASKS:\n- Easier to track progress\n- Can resume if interrupted\n- Better error handling (failure of one task doesn't affect others)\n- Parallel work possible in future\n\nAVAILABLE TOOLS (use exact XML format):\n- <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>High-level goal and context</instructions></createPlan> - Create the plan FIRST\n- <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>Detailed step-by-step instruction for the model to follow when executing this task</instruction></createTask> - Add tasks AFTER creating plan\n- <updateTask><id>taskId</id><status>pending|completed|blocked</status></updateTask> - Update task status\n- <deleteTask><id>taskId</id></deleteTask> - Remove a task\n- <clearAllTasks/> - Remove ALL tasks from the current plan\n- <cancelPlan/> - Cancel and delete the current plan entirely\n- <viewTask/> or <viewTask><id>taskId</id></viewTask> - View plan or specific task\n- <listTasks/> - List all tasks in current plan\n- <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView> - Show directory tree. Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n\nTOOL USAGE GUIDELINES:\n(NOTE: The writing/editing tools below \u2014 Terminal, WriteFile, AppendFile, ReplaceLine, etc. \u2014 are BUILD-mode only. In PLAN mode they will be rejected. Use only plan tools listed above.)\n- Terminal: Use ONLY for one-liner commands. For complex scripts or data processing, use WriteFile/CreateFile.\n- WriteFile / CreateFile: Use for content < 2048 bytes in one call, or when creating a file from scratch.\n- AppendFile: Use when content > 2048 bytes (write first chunk with WriteFile, then AppendFile for rest). Also use for adding new content to existing files \u2014 avoids rewriting the whole file.\n- ReplaceLine: Use for targeted line edits. Specify a single line or a range of lines to replace with new content. Prefer this over WriteFile when you only need to change specific lines.\n  **CRITICAL ReplaceLine rules:**\n  - The parameter is <replacement>, NOT <content> or <contentOfFile>. WRONG: <content>Hello</content> -> ERROR. RIGHT: <replacement>Hello</replacement>\n  - Always ReadFile first to count lines and get exact line numbers (1-indexed)\n  - When replacing a block (CSS rule, function, class), include BOTH the opening AND closing delimiters in the range\n  - Example: to replace a block on lines 15-22, set fromLine=15, toLine=22\n  - After ReplaceLine, use ReadFile to verify the result looks correct\n  - **Edge case \u2014 last block in file**: When editing the final block (e.g. `if __name__ == \"__main__\":`), include the block header in the `fromLine`..`toLine` range. If you replace only the indented body, the header is left orphaned. Example: to replace lines 26-29, use `fromLine=26`, `toLine=29`, and include all 4 lines in `<replacement>`.\n  - If unsure about line range, replace fewer lines and iterate\n  - Multi-line replacement: put raw newlines inside <replacement>...</replacement>. Replacing 1 line with N lines shifts later line numbers by N-1.\n\n  ReplaceLine examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>12</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- TreeView: Use to explore project directory structure. Set depth=0 for unlimited depth.\n- General Rule: NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Grep / Find / List / TreeView: Prefer these XML tools over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- EDITING MINDSET: Just as planning splits a big job into small focused tasks, split big file writes into small targeted edits. Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. Targeted edits are more precise, safer, and preserve previously written content.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW:\n1. User says: \"I want a web app with login and dashboard\"\n2. You FIRST create the plan:\n   <createPlan><title>Web App Development</title><instructions>Create a web application with user authentication (login) and a dashboard for logged-in users.</instructions></createPlan>\n3. Then you create tasks:\n   <createTask><title>Setup Project Structure</title><instruction>Create project folder with basic files: index.html, style.css, app.js, server.py. Initialize npm if needed.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Create Backend API</title><instruction>Create server.py with Flask/FastAPI. Add login endpoint /api/login that validates username/password and returns JWT token. Add /api/dashboard endpoint that requires auth.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Build Frontend Login</title><instruction>Create index.html with login form. Connect to /api/login. Store JWT token in localStorage. Redirect to dashboard on success.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Build Dashboard</title><instruction>Create dashboard view. Fetch user data from /api/dashboard with token. Display user info and logout button.</instruction></createTask>\n\nWhen all tasks are created, tell the user \"Plan is ready! Type !MODE build to start BUILD mode.\"\n", "sessionId": 318, "rowId": 64, "timestamp": 1783654758.8736055, "date": "2026-07-10"} -->

Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n\nTOOL USAGE GUIDELINES:\n(NOTE: The writing/editing tools below \u2014 Terminal, WriteFile, AppendFile, ReplaceLine, etc. \u2014 are BUILD-mode only. In PLAN mode they will be rejected. Use only plan tools listed above.)\n- Terminal: Use ONLY for one-liner commands. For complex scripts or data processing, use WriteFile/CreateFile.\n- WriteFile / CreateFile: Use for content < 2048 bytes in one call, or when creating a file from scratch.\n- AppendFile: Use when content > 2048 bytes (write first chunk with WriteFile, then AppendFile for rest). Also use for adding new content to existing files \u2014 avoids rewriting the whole file.\n- ReplaceLine: Use for targeted line edits. Specify a single line or a range of lines to replace with new content. Prefer this over WriteFile when you only need to change specific lines.\n  **CRITICAL ReplaceLine rules:**\n  - The parameter is <replacement>, NOT <content> or <contentOfFile>. WRONG: <content>Hello</content> -> ERROR. RIGHT: <replacement>Hello</replacement>\n  - Always ReadFile first to count lines and get exact line numbers (1-indexed)\n  - When replacing a block (CSS rule, function, class), include BOTH the opening AND closing delimiters in the range\n  - Example: to replace a block on lines 15-22, set fromLine=15, toLine=22\n  - After ReplaceLine, use ReadFile to verify the result looks correct\n  - **Edge case \u2014 last block in file**: When editing the final block (e.g. `if __name__ == \"__main__\":`), include the block header in the `fromLine`..`toLine` range. If you replace only the indented body, the header is left orphaned. Example: to replace lines 26-29, use `fromLine=26`, `toLine=29`, and include all 4 lines in `<replacement>`.\n  - If unsure about line range, replace fewer lines and iterate\n  - Multi-line replacement: put raw newlines inside <replacement>...</replacement>. Replacing 1 line with N lines shifts later line numbers by N-1.\n\n  ReplaceLine examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>12</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- TreeView: Use to explore project directory structure. Set depth=0 for unlimited depth.\n- General Rule: NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Grep / Find / List / TreeView: Prefer these XML tools over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- EDITING MINDSET: Just as planning splits a big job into small focused tasks, split big file writes into small targeted edits. Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. Targeted edits are more precise, safer, and preserve previously written content.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW:\n1. User says: \"I want a web app with login and dashboard\"\n2. os.path.join(dest_dir, new_name)\n                counter += 1\n        \n        try:\n            if os.path.isdir(self._clipboard):\n                shutil.copytree(self._clipboard, dest_path)\n            else:\n                shutil.copy2(self._clipboard, dest_path)\n            self.status_bar.update(f\"Pasted: {os.path.basename(dest_path)}\")\n            self._refresh_file_view()\n {e}\")\n            \n    def _on_context_remove(self, path):\n        \"\"\"Remove file or directory with confirmation.\"\"\"\n        if not path:\n            return\n            \n        name = \n    def _toggle_status_bar(self):\n        \"\"\"Toggle status bar visibility.\"\"\"\n        if self.menu_bar.get_show_status_var().get():\n            self.status_bar.show()\n        else:\n    x = self.config[\"window\"][\"x\"]\n        y = self.config[\"window\"][\"y\"]\n        self.root.geometry(f\"{width}x{height}+{x}+{y}\")\n        \n    def _on_window_close(self):\n        \"\"\"Handle window close event.\"\"\"\n        # Cancel any pending sash save timer\n        if self._sash_save_timer:\n            self.root.after_cancel(self._sash_save_timer)\n \"\"\"Save current window state to config.\"\"\"\n        geometry = self.root.geometry()\n        try:\n            size, x, y = geometry.split('+')\n            width, height = size.split('x')\n            self.config[\"window\"][\"width\"] = int(width)\n            self.config[\"window\"][\"height\"] = int(height)\n            self.config[\"window\"][\"x\"] = int(x)\n            self.config[\"window\"][\"y\"] = int(y)\n        except ValueError:\n            pass\n            \n        # Also save sash position as backup\n        if hasattr(self, 'paned_window'):\n self.config_manager.save_config(self.config)\n        \n    def _bind_sash_save(self):\n        \"\"\"Bind to sash movement to save panel width.\"\"\"\n        self.paned_window.bind('<ButtonRelease-1>', self._on_sash_release)\n        \n    def _on_sash_release(self, event):\n        \"\"\"Handle sash release - save position after a delay.\"\"\"\n        if      \n                except (OSError, PermissionError):\n                    continue\n                    \n            total = file_count + dir_count\n            self.status_bar.update(f\"{total}         else:\n                shutil.copy2(self._clipboard, dest_path)\n            self.status_bar.update(f\"Pasted: {os.path.basename(dest_path)}\")\n            self._refresh_file_view()\n <!-- {"role": "system", "content": "\nYou are in PLAN MODE. You are architect. Your role is to analyze user requests and create structured task plans.\n\nMODE: PLAN (Thinking ENABLED)\n\nIMPORTANT WORKFLOW:\n\nPHASE 0 - CONTEXT GATHERING (MANDATORY):\nBefore creating ANY plan, you MUST understand the existing codebase:\n1. Call <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView> to see project structure\n2. Call <ReadFile><fileName>README.md</fileName></ReadFile> to understand the project\n3. Call <ReadFile><fileName>AGENTS.md</fileName></ReadFile> to understand conventions\n4. List and read key config files (package.json, requirements.txt, config.py, etc.)\n5. Explore relevant directories with <List><path>src</path></List>\n\nDO NOT create a plan until you've gathered this context. The user may provide files to read directly.\n\nPHASE 1 - CREATE PLAN:\nCall <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>High-level goal description</instructions></createPlan>\n\nPHASE 2 - CREATE TASKS:\nCall <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>Detailed instruction for this task</instruction></createTask> for each step\n\nPHASE 3 - FINALIZE:\nWhen all tasks are created, tell user: \"Plan is ready! Type !MODE build to start BUILD mode.\"\n\nHOW TO SPLIT USER INSTRUCTIONS INTO TASKS:\n1. Analyze the user's goal - what is the end result they want?\n2. Identify distinct steps that can be done independently\n3. Create tasks for each step with clear, actionable instructions\n4. Order matters - earlier tasks should enable later ones\n5. Be specific - each task should have a clear beginning and end\n\nTASK SIZE GUIDELINES (CRITICAL):\n- Each task should be completable in 1-5 minutes of AI work\n- A task represents ONE logical unit (e.g., \"Create login form\" not \"Build entire auth system\")\n- If a task requires >3 file edits, split it into smaller tasks\n- Tasks should be independently verifiable\n- Prefer 5-10 small tasks over 1-2 large ones\n- Each task should have clear success criteria\n\nWHY SPLIT INTO TASKS:\n- Easier to track progress\n- Can resume if interrupted\n- Better error handling (failure of one task doesn't affect others)\n- Parallel work possible in future\n\nAVAILABLE TOOLS (use exact XML format):\n- <createPlan><title>Plan Title</title><instructions>High-level goal and context</instructions></createPlan> - Create the plan FIRST\n- <createTask><title>Task Title</title><instruction>Detailed step-by-step instruction for the model to follow when executing this task</instruction></createTask> - Add tasks AFTER creating plan\n- <updateTask><id>taskId</id><status>pending|completed|blocked</status></updateTask> - Update task status\n- <deleteTask><id>taskId</id></deleteTask> - Remove a task\n- <clearAllTasks/> - Remove ALL tasks from the current plan\n- <cancelPlan/> - Cancel and delete the current plan entirely\n- <viewTask/> or <viewTask><id>taskId</id></viewTask> - View plan or specific task\n- <listTasks/> - List all tasks in current plan\n- <TreeView><path>.</path><depth>3</depth></TreeView> - Show directory tree. Params: [<path>], [<depth>] (default 3), [<pattern>] (glob filter), [<showHidden>]\n\nTOOL USAGE GUIDELINES:\n(NOTE: The writing/editing tools below \u2014 Terminal, WriteFile, AppendFile, ReplaceLine, etc. \u2014 are BUILD-mode only. In PLAN mode they will be rejected. Use only plan tools listed above.)\n- Terminal: Use ONLY for one-liner commands. For complex scripts or data processing, use WriteFile/CreateFile.\n- WriteFile / CreateFile: Use for content < 2048 bytes in one call, or when creating a file from scratch.\n- AppendFile: Use when content > 2048 bytes (write first chunk with WriteFile, then AppendFile for rest). Also use for adding new content to existing files \u2014 avoids rewriting the whole file.\n- ReplaceLine: Use for targeted line edits. Specify a single line or a range of lines to replace with new content. Prefer this over WriteFile when you only need to change specific lines.\n  **CRITICAL ReplaceLine rules:**\n  - The parameter is <replacement>, NOT <content> or <contentOfFile>. WRONG: <content>Hello</content> -> ERROR. RIGHT: <replacement>Hello</replacement>\n  - Always ReadFile first to count lines and get exact line numbers (1-indexed)\n  - When replacing a block (CSS rule, function, class), include BOTH the opening AND closing delimiters in the range\n  - Example: to replace a block on lines 15-22, set fromLine=15, toLine=22\n  - After ReplaceLine, use ReadFile to verify the result looks correct\n  - **Edge case \u2014 last block in file**: When editing the final block (e.g. `if __name__ == \"__main__\":`), include the block header in the `fromLine`..`toLine` range. If you replace only the indented body, the header is left orphaned. Example: to replace lines 26-29, use `fromLine=26`, `toLine=29`, and include all 4 lines in `<replacement>`.\n  - If unsure about line range, replace fewer lines and iterate\n  - Multi-line replacement: put raw newlines inside <replacement>...</replacement>. Replacing 1 line with N lines shifts later line numbers by N-1.\n\n  ReplaceLine examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>12</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- TreeView: Use to explore project directory structure. Set depth=0 for unlimited depth.\n- General Rule: NEVER call multiple tool calls for large content. Split large data: WriteFile first chunk -> AppendFile remaining.\n- Grep / Find / List / TreeView: Prefer these XML tools over Terminal commands (grep, find, ls).\n- XML Content: Never use backslashes to escape characters inside XML values \u2014 the parser handles special characters natively. Write raw content without escaping quotes (write `\"Hello\"` not `\"Hello\"`).\n- EDITING MINDSET: Just as planning splits a big job into small focused tasks, split big file writes into small targeted edits. Use ReplaceLine for specific line changes and AppendFile for additions instead of rewriting entire files with WriteFile. Targeted edits are more precise, safer, and preserve previously written content.\n\nEXAMPLE WORKFLOW:\n1. User says: \"I want a web app with login and dashboard\"\n2. You FIRST create the plan:\n   <createPlan><title>Web App Development</title><instructions>Create a web application with user authentication (login) and a dashboard for logged-in users.</instructions></createPlan>\n3. Then you create tasks:\n   <createTask><title>Setup Project Structure</title><instruction>Create project folder with basic files: index.html, style.css, app.js, server.py. Initialize npm if needed.</instruction></createTask>\n   <createTask><title>Create Backend API</title><instruction>Create server.py with Flask/FastAPI. Params: <fileName>, [<prompt>]\n- <ExecuteScript><fileName>ls</fileName><args>-l</args></ExecuteScript>: Run script (.py, .sh, .js, etc). Params: <fileName>, [<args>]\n- <Grep><pattern>search_term</pattern><fileName>file.txt</fileName><recursive>true</recursive></Grep>: Search by regex. Prefer this over Terminal grep. Use for targeted edits instead of rewriting the whole file. Multi-line replacements shift later line numbers.\n\n  Examples:\n  Single line:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>config.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>5</fromLine>\n    <replacement>DEBUG = True</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n\n  Multi-line block:\n  <ReplaceLine>\n    <fileName>app.py</fileName>\n    <fromLine>10</fromLine>\n    <toLine>15</toLine>\n    <replacement>def new_function():\n      print(\"new code\")\n      return 42</replacement>\n  </ReplaceLine>\n- <Find><pattern>*.py</pattern><path>.</path></Find>: Find by name. Prefer this over Terminal find. Params: <pattern>, [<path>]\n- <Head><fileName>file.txt</fileName><lines>10</lines></Head>: First N lines. <!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "<WriteFile>\n<fileName>README.md</fileName>\n<contentOfFile>\n# KosFM\n\nA simple, cross-platform file manager built with Python and tkinter. Features a dual-pane interface with a resizable directory tree on the left and file listing on the right. Now with Linux desktop integration via xdg-mime!\n\n![Python Version](https://img.shields.io/badge/python-3.6+-blue.svg)\n![License](https://img.shields.io/badge/license-MIT-green.svg)\n![Platform](https://img.shields.io/badge/platform-Linux%20%7C%20Windows%20%7C%20macOS-lightgrey.svg)\n\n## Features\n\n- **Dual-Pane Interface**: Resizable directory tree on the left, file listing on the right\n- **Linux Desktop Integration**: Full xdg-mime support for file associations\n- **File Operations**: Copy, Paste, Rename, and Remove files/directories\n- **Context Menu**: Right-click menu with Open, Open With, Copy, Paste, Rename, Remove, Copy Path, Properties\n- **Panel Width Persistence**: Panel sizes are saved and restored between sessions\n- **File Opening**: Double-click to open files with default application\n- **Open With**: Choose from available applications and set defaults\n- **Application Detection**: Automatically finds all apps that can handle a file type\n- **Saved Preferences**: Remembers your \"Open With\" choices between sessions\n- **Lazy Loading**: Directories load on-demand for better performance\n- **File Details**: View file size, modification date, and type\n- **Resizable Panels**: Drag the divider to adjust panel widths\n- **Navigation**: \n  - Click directories in tree to view contents\n  - Double-click folders to navigate into them\n  - \"Up\" button to go to parent directory\n  - Path bar for direct navigation\n- **Menu Bar**: File, View, and Help menus with keyboard shortcuts\n- **View Options**: Toggle hidden files and status bar visibility\n- **Window State**: Saves position, size, and panel widths between sessions\n- **Icons**: Visual distinction with emoji icons (\ud83d\udcc1 folders, \ud83d\udcc4 files)\n- **Cross-Platform**: Works on Windows, macOS, and Linux\n- **Error Handling**: Graceful handling of permission errors and inaccessible directories\n- **Status Bar**: Shows item count and current path\n\n## File Operations\n\nKosFM now includes full file operation support:\n\n- **Copy** - Copy file/directory to clipboard\n- **Paste** - Paste into current directory (auto-handles duplicates with suffix)\n- **Rename** - Rename files and directories with dialog\n- **Remove** - Delete files and directories with confirmation\n\nAll operations include proper error handling and user confirmation for destructive actions.\n\n## File Opening (Linux)\n\nKosFM integrates with your Linux desktop environment using `xdg-mime`:\n\n- **Double-click** any file to open with its default application\n- **Right-click** \u2192 \"Open With...\" to choose from available applications\n- **Set as default** checkbox to make an app the default for that file type\n- **Saved preferences** persist between sessions in `config.json`\n\nSupported features:\n- MIME type detection via `xdg-mime query filetype`\n- Application discovery from `/usr/share/applications` and `~/.local/share/applications`\n- .desktop file parsing (Name, Icon, Exec, MimeType)\n- Field code handling (%f, %F, %u, %U in Exec lines)\n- System-wide default setting via `xdg-mime default`\n\n## Project Structure\n\n```\nKosFM/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 main.py                 # Entry point\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 install.py              # Installation script\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 KosFM/                  # Main \u2514\u2500\u2500 utils/              # Utility modules\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 __init__.py\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 config_manager.py # Config save/load\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 error_handler.py  # Error handling\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 file_utils.py     # File formatting\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 platform_utils.py # Platform-specific code\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 xdg_mime.py       # Linux MIME type handling\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 README.md               # This file\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 CHANGELOG.md            # Version history\n```\n\n## Requirements\n\n- Python 3.6 or higher\n- tkinter (included with Python standard library)\n\n## Installation\n\n1. Clone or download this repository\n2. Run the installer:\n   ```bash\n   ./install.py --install\n   ```\n3. Or run directly:\n   ```bash\n   python main.py\n   ```\n\n## Usage\n\nRun the file manager:\n\n```bash\nkosfm\n# or\npython main.py\n```\n\n### Navigation\n\n| Action | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| Click folder in tree | View contents in right panel |\n| Double-click folder | Navigate into folder |\n| Double-click file | Open file with default application |\n| Click \"Up\" button | Go to parent directory |\n| Type path + Enter | Navigate to specific path |\n| Click \"Refresh\" | Reload current directory |\n| Drag divider | Resize left/right panels (size is saved) |\n\n### Context Menu (Right-Click)\n\n| Option | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| Open | Open file with default application |\n| Open With... | Choose application to open file |\n| Copy | Copy file/directory to clipboard |\n| Paste | Paste from clipboard to current directory |\n| Rename | Rename file or directory |\n| Remove | Delete file or directory (with confirmation) |\n| Copy Path | Copy full path to clipboard |\n| Properties | Show file details |\n\n### Keyboard Shortcuts\n\n| Shortcut | Action |\n|----------|--------|\n| Ctrl+R | Refresh current directory |\n| Ctrl+Q | Exit application |\n\n## Menu Bar\n\n### File Menu\n| Option | Shortcut | Description |\n|--------|----------|-------------|\n| Refresh | Ctrl+R | Reload current directory |\n| Exit | Ctrl+Q | Close application |\n\n### View Menu\n| Option | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| Show Hidden Files | Toggle visibility of hidden files (.*) |\n| Show Status Bar | Toggle status bar at bottom |\n\n### Help Menu\n| Option | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| Keyboard Shortcuts | Show all available shortcuts |\n| About | Application information |\n\n## Configuration\n\nConfiguration is automatically saved to `~/.config/KosFM/config.json` and includes:\n- Window position and size\n- Panel divider position (saved automatically when resized)\n- View options (show hidden files, show status bar)\n- MIME type application preferences (saved \"Open With\" choices)\n\n## Platform Support\n\n| Platform | Status | Notes |\n|----------|--------|-------|\n| Linux | \u2705 Supported | Full xdg-mime integration, file operations |\n| Windows | \u2705 Supported | Shows all drives (C:\\, D:\\, etc.) |\n| macOS | \u2705 Supported | Shows / and /Users |\n\n## Modular Architecture\n\nThe application is organized into focused modules:\n\n- **main.py**: Minimal entry point\n- **KosFM/app.py**: Main application controller\n- **KosFM/dialogs.py**: Dialog handlers (Open With, Properties)\n- **KosFM/navigation.py**: Navigation logic\n- **KosFM/ui/**: Self-contained UI widgets\n- **KosFM/utils/**: Reusable utility functions\n- **KosFM/config.py**: Centralized constants\n\nThis structure makes the code easy to maintain, test, and extend.\n\n## Future Enhancements\n\n- [ ] File preview panel\n- [ ] Search <!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "<WriteFile>\n<fileName>CHANGELOG.md</fileName>\n<contentOfFile>\n# Changelog\n\nAll notable changes to KosFM will be documented in this file.\n\nThe format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.0.0/),\nand this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).\n\n## [1.4.0] - 2026-07-09\n\n### Added\n- **File Operations**: Full file management support\n  - **Copy**: Copy files/directories to clipboard\n  - **Paste**: Paste into current directory with auto-renaming for duplicates\n  - **Rename**: Rename files and directories with dialog\n  - **Remove**: Delete files and directories with confirmation dialog\n- **Panel Width Persistence**: Panel divider position is now saved automatically\n  - Saves when you stop dragging the divider (500ms debounce)\n  - Restores position on application startup\n  - Also saves on window close as backup\n- **Context Menu Improvements**: Menu now closes when clicking outside of it\n  - Added `<FocusOut>` binding to auto-close menu\n  - Clicking on tree view closes any open menu\n\n### Changed\n- **Code Refactoring**: Split large app.py into focused modules\n  - New `dialogs.py` module for OpenWithDialog and PropertiesDialog\n  - New `navigation.py` module for NavigationManager\n  - `app.py` is now a thinner controller (~400 lines vs ~600)\n- **File Opening**: Changed from single-click to double-click\n  - Single-click now just selects the file\n  - Double-click opens files or navigates into folders\n  - Prevents accidental file opening\n\n### Fixed\n- Context menu staying open when clicking elsewhere\n- Panel width not persisting between sessions properly\n\n## [1.3.0] - 2026-07-09\n\n### Added\n- **Linux xdg-mime Integration**: Full support for Linux desktop file associations\n  - MIME type detection via `xdg-mime query filetype`\n  - Automatic discovery of applications from .desktop files\n  - Single-click file opening with default application\n  - \"Open With\" dialog showing all apps for a file type\n  - \"Set as default\" checkbox to save preferences\n  - Saved preferences persist in config.json\n  - System-wide default setting via `xdg-mime default`\n- **Right-Click Context Menu**: New context menu on files with options:\n  - **Open**: Open file with default application\n  - **Open With...**: Choose from available applications\n  - **Copy Path**: Copy file path to clipboard\n  - **Properties**: Show file details dialog\n- **New Utils Module**: `xdg_mime.py` with functions:\n  - `get_mime_type()` - Detect MIME type\n  - `get_default_application()` - Get default app\n  - `set_default_application()` - Set system default\n  - `find_applications_for_mime_type()` - Find all compatible apps\n  - `parse_desktop_file()` - Parse .desktop files\n  - `launch_application()` - Launch with specific app\n  - `open_file_with_default()` - Open via xdg-open\n\n### Changed\n- **File Opening**: Now uses xdg-mime on Linux for proper file associations\n- **Config**: Added `mime_apps` section for saved application preferences\n- **App**: Updated `_on_file_click()` to check saved preferences before opening\n\n### Technical\n- Scans `/usr/share/applications`, `/usr/local/share/applications`, and `~/.local/share/applications`\n- Handles .desktop field codes (%f, %F, %u, %U)\n- Supports wildcard MIME type matching (e.g., `image/*` matches `image/png`)\n- Filters out NoDisplay and Hidden apps\n\n## [1.2.0] - 2026-07-09\n\n### Added\n- **Window State Persistence**: Saves and restores:\n  - Window position (x, y)\n  - Window size (width, height)\n  - Panel divider position\n  - View options (hidden files, status bar visibility)\n  - Stored in `~/.config/KosFM/config.json`\n\n### Changed\n- **Project Structure**: Complete reorganization\n  - `main.py`: Now a minimal 27-line entry point\n  - `KosFM/app.py`: Main application controller\n  - `KosFM/ui/`: Tree panel, file panel, menu bar, status bar widgets\n  - `KosFM/utils/`: Config manager, error handler, file utils, platform utils\n- Improved code organization and maintainability\n- Better separation of concerns\n\n### Technical Details\n- Uses relative imports within the package\n- ConfigManager handles JSON config in ~/.config/KosFM/\n- Each UI component is self-contained with clear interfaces\n- Platform utilities abstract OS-specific code\n\n## [1.1.0] - 2026-07-09\n\n### Added\n- **Menu Bar** with three menus:\n  - **File Menu**: Refresh (Ctrl+R), Exit (Ctrl+Q)\n  - **View Menu**: \n    - Show/Hide Hidden Files toggle\n    - Show/Hide Status Bar toggle\n  - **Help Menu**: Keyboard Shortcuts dialog, About dialog\n- Hidden files filtering (files starting with `.`)\n- Status bar visibility toggle\n- Keyboard shortcuts for menu actions\n\n## [1.0.0] - 2026-07-09\n\n### Added\n- Initial release of KosFM\n- Dual-pane interface with directory tree and file listing\n- Left panel: Directory tree with lazy loading\n  - Platform-aware root directories (Windows drives / Unix root)\n  - Expandable folders with on-demand loading\n  - Folder icons (\ud83d\udcc1) for visual distinction\n- Right panel: File listing with details\n  - Columns: Name, Size, Modified Date, Type\n  - Sorts folders first, then alphabetically\n  - File icons (\ud83d\udcc4) for visual distinction\n- Navigation features\n  - Click tree items to view directory contents\n  - Double-click folders to navigate into them\n  - \"Up\" button for parent directory navigation\n  - Path bar for direct path entry\n  - Refresh button to reload current directory\n- Status bar showing item count and current path\n- Error handling for permission denied and system errors\n- Cross-platform support (Windows, macOS, Linux)\n- Human-readable file sizes (B, KB, MB, GB, TB)\n- Formatted timestamps (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM)\n\n### Technical Details\n- Built with Python 3.6+ and tkinter\n- Uses `os.scandir()` for efficient directory scanning\n- Implements `@handle_error` decorator for consistent error handling\n- Lazy loading prevents freezing on large directories\n- Configurable via `config.py`\n\n## [Unreleased]\n\n### Planned Features\n- File preview panel for images and text\n- Search functionality across directories\n- Bookmarks and favorites\n- Dark theme support\n- Additional keyboard shortcuts (F5 refresh, Ctrl+C copy, etc.)\n- Different icons for different file types\n- Drag and drop support\n- Multi-select for batch operations\n\n---\n\n## Version > Menu bar widget for KosFM.

>     """Application menu bar."""

>         """
>         Initialize menu bar.
>         
>         Args:
>             root: Root window
>             handlers: Dict with callback functions for menu items
>                 - refresh: Called for Refresh
>       ...
